<p><b>QuickTime</b> is an extensible <a href="/wiki/Multimedia_framework" title="Multimedia framework">multimedia framework</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a>, capable of handling various formats of <a href="/wiki/Digital_video" title="Digital video">digital video</a>, picture, sound, <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_VR" title="QuickTime VR">panoramic images</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interactivity" title="Interactivity">interactivity</a>. First made in 1991, the latest Mac version, QuickTime X, is currently available on <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Snow_Leopard" title="Mac OS X Snow Leopard">Mac OS X Snow Leopard</a> and newer. Apple has ceased support for the Windows version of QuickTime in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windows_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Windows-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Lion" title="Mac OS X Lion">Mac OS X Lion</a>, the underlying media framework for QuickTime, QTKit, is deprecated in favor of a newer graphics framework, <a href="/wiki/AVFoundation" title="AVFoundation">AV Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>QuickTime is bundled with macOS. QuickTime for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> is downloadable as a standalone installation, and was bundled with Apple's <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> prior to iTunes 10.5, but is no longer supported and therefore security vulnerabilities will no longer be patched.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windows_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Windows-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">Software development kits</a> (SDK) for QuickTime are available to the public with an <a href="/wiki/Apple_Developer" title="Apple Developer">Apple Developer Connection</a> (ADC) subscription.</p>
<p>It is available free of charge for both macOS and Windows operating systems. There are some other free player applications that rely on the QuickTime framework, providing features not available in the basic QuickTime Player. For example, iTunes can export audio in <a href="/wiki/WAV" title="WAV">WAV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audio_Interchange_File_Format" title="Audio Interchange File Format">AIFF</a>, <a href="/wiki/MP3" title="MP3">MP3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="Advanced Audio Coding">AAC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Lossless" title="Apple Lossless">Apple Lossless</a>. In addition, macOS has a simple <a href="/wiki/AppleScript" title="AppleScript">AppleScript</a> which can be used to play a movie in full-screen mode.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> but since version 7.2 full-screen viewing is now supported in the non-Pro version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_Pro">QuickTime Pro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: QuickTime Pro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>QuickTime Player 7 is limited to only basic playback operations unless a QuickTime Pro license key is purchased from Apple. Until recently, Apple's professional applications (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Final_Cut_Studio" title="Final Cut Studio">Final Cut Studio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logic_Studio" title="Logic Studio">Logic Studio</a>) included a QuickTime Pro license. Pro keys are specific to the major version of QuickTime for which they are purchased and unlock additional features of the QuickTime Player application on macOS or Windows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The Pro key does not require any additional downloads; entering the registration code immediately unlocks the hidden features.</p>
<p>Features enabled by the Pro license include, but are not limited to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Editing clips through the cut, copy and paste functions, merging separate audio and video tracks, and freely placing the video tracks on a virtual canvas with the options of cropping and rotation.</li>
<li>Saving and exporting (<a href="/wiki/Encoder" title="Encoder">encoding</a>) to any of the <a href="/wiki/Video_codec" title="Video codec">codecs</a> supported by QuickTime. QuickTime 7 includes presets for exporting video to a video-capable <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>.</li>
<li>Saving existing QuickTime movies from the web directly to a hard disk drive. This is often, but not always, either hidden or intentionally blocked in the standard mode. It should be noted that two options exist for saving movies from a web browser:
<ul>
<li>Save as source – This option will save the embedded video in its original format. (I.e. not limited to .mov files.)</li>
<li>Save as QuickTime movie – This option will save the embedded video in a .mov file format no matter what the original container is/was.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Snow_Leopard" title="Mac OS X Snow Leopard">Mac OS X Snow Leopard</a> includes QuickTime X. QuickTime Player X lacks cut, copy and paste and will only export to four formats, but its limited export feature is free. Users do not have an option to upgrade to a Pro version of QuickTime X, but those who have already purchased QuickTime 7 Pro and are upgrading to Snow Leopard from a previous version of Mac OS X will have QuickTime 7 stored in the Utilities or user defined folder. Otherwise, users will have to install QuickTime 7 from the "Optional Installs" directory of the Snow Leopard DVD after installing the OS.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Lion" title="Mac OS X Lion">Mac OS X Lion</a> and later also include QuickTime X. No installer for QuickTime 7 is included with these software packages, but users can download the QuickTime 7 installer from the <a class="external text" href="http://support.apple.com/kb/DL923" rel="nofollow">Apple support</a> site.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_framework">QuickTime framework</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: QuickTime framework">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The QuickTime framework provides the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Encoding and <a href="/wiki/Transcoding" title="Transcoding">transcoding</a> video and audio from one format to another.</li>
<li>Decoding video and audio, then sending the decoded stream to the graphics or audio subsystem for playback. In macOS, QuickTime sends video playback to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quartz_Extreme" title="Quartz Extreme">Quartz Extreme (OpenGL) Compositor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li>A "component" plug-in architecture for supporting additional 3rd-party codecs (such as <a href="/wiki/DivX" title="DivX">DivX</a>).</li>
</ul>
<p>As of early 2008, the framework hides many older codecs listed below<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)"><span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2011)">where?</span></a></i>]</sup> from the user although the option to "Show legacy encoders" exists in QuickTime Preferences to use them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The framework supports the following file types and codecs natively:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="PictureViewer">PictureViewer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: PictureViewer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>PictureViewer</b> is a component of QuickTime for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_8" title="Mac OS 8">Mac OS 8</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_9" title="Mac OS 9">Mac OS 9</a> operating systems. It is used to view picture files from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Still_image" title="Still image">still image</a> formats that QuickTime supports. In <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, it is replaced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preview_(software)" title="Preview (software)">Preview</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon the release of <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> 7.7.7, the Windows version requires one to go to their "Windows Uninstall Or Change A Program" screen to "modify" their installation of QuickTime 7 to include the "Legacy QuickTime Feature" of "QuickTime PictureViewer".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="File_formats">File formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: File formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_File_Format" title="QuickTime File Format">QuickTime File Format</a></div>
<p>The native <a href="/wiki/File_format" title="File format">file format</a> for QuickTime video, <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_File_Format" title="QuickTime File Format">QuickTime File Format</a>, specifies a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Container_format_(digital)" title="Container format (digital)">multimedia container file</a> that contains one or more tracks, each of which stores a particular type of data: audio, video, effects, or text (e.g. for subtitles). Each track either contains a digitally encoded media stream (using a specific format) or a data reference to the media stream located in another file. The ability to contain abstract data references for the media data, and the separation of the media data from the media offsets and the track edit lists means that QuickTime is particularly suited for editing, as it is capable of importing and editing in place (without data copying).</p>
<p>Other file formats that QuickTime supports natively (to varying degrees) include <a href="/wiki/Audio_Interchange_File_Format" title="Audio Interchange File Format">AIFF</a>, <a href="/wiki/WAV" title="WAV">WAV</a>, <a href="/wiki/DV" title="DV">DV-DIF</a>, <a href="/wiki/MP3" title="MP3">MP3</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MPEG_program_stream" title="MPEG program stream">MPEG program stream</a>. With additional QuickTime Components, it can also support <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Systems_Format" title="Advanced Systems Format">ASF</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DivX_Media_Format" title="DivX Media Format">DivX Media Format</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">Flash Video</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matroska" title="Matroska">Matroska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ogg" title="Ogg">Ogg</a>, and many others.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_and_MPEG-4">QuickTime and MPEG-4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: QuickTime and MPEG-4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On February 11, 1998, the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">ISO</a> approved the QuickTime file format as the basis of the MPEG‑4 file format.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="MPEG-4 file format was published as ISO standard in 2001 and QuickTime format used as basis was also published in 2001. Does ISO really approved QuickTime format as the basis for MP4 in 1998? (June 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The MPEG-4 file format specification was created on the basis of the QuickTime format specification published in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quicktime-format-2001_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-quicktime-format-2001-14">[14]</a></sup> The MP4 (<tt>.mp4</tt>) file format was published in 2001 as the revision of the MPEG-4 Part 1: Systems specification published in 1999 (ISO/IEC 14496-1:2001).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalpreservation-ISO-14496-1-2001_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalpreservation-ISO-14496-1-2001-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfc4337_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-rfc4337-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISO-14496-1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISO-14496-1-17">[17]</a></sup> In 2003, the first version of MP4 format was revised and replaced by <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4_Part_14" title="MPEG-4 Part 14">MPEG-4 Part 14</a>: MP4 file format (ISO/IEC 14496-14:2003).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISO-14496-14_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISO-14496-14-18">[18]</a></sup> The MP4 file format was generalized into the <a href="/wiki/ISO_base_media_file_format" title="ISO base media file format">ISO Base Media File Format</a> ISO/IEC 14496-12:2004, which defines a general structure for time-based media files. It in turn is used as the basis for other multimedia file formats (for example <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3GP" title="3GP">3GP</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MJ2" title="MJ2">Motion JPEG 2000</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mp4ra-org-references_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-mp4ra-org-references-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mpeg4part12_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-mpeg4part12-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mpeg4part12--new_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-mpeg4part12--new-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mpeg4part12-mp4_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-mpeg4part12-mp4-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISO-14496-12_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISO-14496-12-23">[23]</a></sup> A list of all registered extensions for ISO Base Media File Format is published on the official registration authority website <a class="external text" href="http://www.mp4ra.org" rel="nofollow">www.mp4ra.org</a>. This registration authority for code-points in "MP4 Family" files is Apple Computer Inc. and it is named in Annex D (informative) in MPEG-4 Part 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mpeg4part12-mp4_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-mpeg4part12-mp4-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 2000, MPEG-4 formats became industry standards, first appearing with support in QuickTime 6 in 2002. Accordingly, the MPEG-4 container is designed to capture, edit, <a href="/wiki/Archive" title="Archive">archive</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Distribution_(business)" title="Distribution (business)">distribute</a> media, unlike the simple file-as-stream approach of MPEG-1 and <a href="/wiki/MPEG-2" title="MPEG-2">MPEG-2</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Profile_support">Profile support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Profile support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>QuickTime 6 added limited support for MPEG-4; specifically encoding and decoding using Simple Profile (SP). Advanced Simple Profile (ASP) features, like <a href="/wiki/Video_compression_picture_types" title="Video compression picture types">B-frames</a>, were unsupported (in contrast with, for example, encoders such as <a href="/wiki/Xvid" title="Xvid">XviD</a> or <a href="/wiki/3ivx" title="3ivx">3ivx</a>). QuickTime 7 supports the H.264 encoder and decoder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Container_benefits">Container benefits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Container benefits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Because both MOV and MP4 containers can use the same MPEG-4 codecs, they are mostly interchangeable in a QuickTime-only environment. MP4, being an international standard, has more support. This is especially true on hardware devices, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_PSP" title="Sony PSP">Sony PSP</a> and various DVD players; on the software side, most <a href="/wiki/DirectShow" title="DirectShow">DirectShow</a> / <a href="/wiki/Video_for_Windows" title="Video for Windows">Video for Windows</a> codec packs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> include a MP4 parser, but not one for MOV.</p>
<p>In QuickTime Pro's MPEG-4 Export dialog, an option called "Passthrough" allows a clean export to MP4 without affecting the audio or video streams. QuickTime 7 now supports multi-channel AAC-LC and HE-AAC audio (used, for example, in the high-definition trailers on Apple's site<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>), for both .MOV and .MP4 containers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Apple released the first version of QuickTime on December 2, 1991 as a <a href="/wiki/Multimedia" title="Multimedia">multimedia</a> add-on for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/System_Software_6" title="System Software 6">System Software 6</a> and later. The lead developer of QuickTime, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Leak" title="Bruce Leak">Bruce Leak</a>, ran the first public demonstration at the May 1991 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Worldwide_Developers_Conference" title="Worldwide Developers Conference">Worldwide Developers Conference</a>, where he played Apple's famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1984_(television_commercial)" title="1984 (television commercial)">1984 TV commercial</a> in a window at 320×240 pixels resolution.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_1.x">QuickTime 1.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: QuickTime 1.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The original video <a href="/wiki/Codec" title="Codec">codecs</a> included:</p>
<ul>
<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animation_codec" title="Animation codec">Animation codec</a>, which used <a href="/wiki/Run-length_encoding" title="Run-length encoding">run-length encoding</a> and better suited cartoon-type images with large areas of flat color</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Video" title="Apple Video">Apple Video</a> codec (also known as "Road Pizza"), suited to normal live-action video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_Graphics" title="QuickTime Graphics">Graphics</a> codec, for 8-bit images, including ones that had undergone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dithering" title="Dithering">dithering</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The first commercial project produced using QuickTime 1.0 was the CD-ROM <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070607104108/http://www.againstallodds.com/alice.htm" rel="nofollow">From Alice to Ocean</a>. The first publicly visible use of QuickTime was <a href="/wiki/Ben_%26_Jerry%27s" title="Ben &amp; Jerry's">Ben &amp; Jerry's</a> interactive factory tour (dubbed <i>The Rik &amp; Joe Show</i> after its in-house developers). <i>The Rik and Joe Show</i> was demonstrated onstage at MacWorld in San Francisco when <a href="/wiki/John_Sculley" title="John Sculley">John Sculley</a> announced QuickTime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Apple released QuickTime 1.5 for Mac OS in the latter part of 1992. This added the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SuperMac" title="SuperMac">SuperMac</a>-developed <a href="/wiki/Cinepak" title="Cinepak">Cinepak</a> vector-quantization video codec (initially known as Compact Video). It could play video at 320×240 resolution at 30 frames per second on a 25 MHz <a href="/wiki/Motorola_68040" title="Motorola 68040">Motorola 68040</a> CPU. It also added <i>text</i> tracks, which allowed for captioning, lyrics and other potential uses.</p>
<p>Apple contracted <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Canyon_Company" title="San Francisco Canyon Company">San Francisco Canyon Company</a> to port QuickTime to the Windows platform. Version 1.0 of QuickTime for Windows provided only a subset of the full QuickTime API, including only movie playback functions driven through the standard movie controller.</p>
<p>QuickTime 1.6 came out the following year. Version 1.6.2 first incorporated the "QuickTime PowerPlug" which replaced some components with <a href="/wiki/PowerPC" title="PowerPC">PowerPC</a>-native code when running on PowerPC Macs.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_2.x">QuickTime 2.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: QuickTime 2.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quicktime_old_logo.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="215" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Quicktime_old_logo.svg/200px-Quicktime_old_logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Quicktime_old_logo.svg/300px-Quicktime_old_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Quicktime_old_logo.svg/400px-Quicktime_old_logo.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quicktime_old_logo.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Quicktime logo for versions 2.x and 3.x, from 1994 until 1999</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Apple released QuickTime 2.0 for System Software 7 in February 1994—the only version never released for free. It added support for music tracks, which contained the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/MIDI" title="MIDI">MIDI</a> data and which could drive a sound-synthesis engine built into QuickTime itself (using a limited set of instrument sounds licensed from <a href="/wiki/Roland_Corporation" title="Roland Corporation">Roland</a>), or any external MIDI-compatible hardware, thereby producing sounds using only small amounts of movie data.</p>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Leak" title="Bruce Leak">Bruce Leak</a>'s departure to <a href="/wiki/MSN_TV" title="MSN TV">Web TV</a>, the leadership of the QuickTime team was taken over by Peter Hoddie.</p>
<p>QuickTime 2.0 for Windows appeared in November 1994 under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Paul_Charlton_(technologist)" title="Paul Charlton (technologist)">Paul Charlton</a>. As part of the development effort for cross-platform QuickTime, Charlton (as architect and technical lead), along with ace individual contributor Michael Kellner and a small highly effective team including Keith Gurganus, ported a subset of the Macintosh Toolbox to Intel and other platforms (notably, MIPS and SGI Unix variants) as the enabling infrastructure for the QuickTime Media Layer (QTML) which was first demonstrated at the Apple Worldwide Developers Conference (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWDC" title="WWDC">WWDC</a>) in May 1996. The QTML later became the foundation for the Carbon API which allowed legacy Macintosh applications to run on the Darwin kernel in Mac OS X.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The next versions, 2.1 and 2.5, reverted to the previous model of giving QuickTime away for free. They improved the music support and added <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprite_(computer_science)" title="Sprite (computer science)">sprite</a> tracks which allowed the creation of complex animations with the addition of little more than the static sprite images to the size of the movie. QuickTime 2.5 also fully integrated <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_VR" title="QuickTime VR">QuickTime VR</a> 2.0.1 into QuickTime as a QuickTime extension. On January 16, 1997, Apple released the QuickTime MPEG Extension (PPC only) as an add-on to QuickTime 2.5, which added software MPEG-1 playback capabilities to QuickTime.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuit_against_San_Francisco_Canyon">Lawsuit against San Francisco Canyon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Lawsuit against San Francisco Canyon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1994, Apple filed suit against software developer <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Canyon_Company" title="San Francisco Canyon Company">San Francisco Canyon</a> for intellectual property theft and breach of contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Apple alleged that San Francisco Canyon had helped develop <a href="/wiki/Video_for_Windows" title="Video for Windows">Video for Windows</a> using several thousand lines of stolen QuickTime source code. Microsoft and Intel were added to the lawsuit in 1995. The suit ended in a settlement in 1997.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_3.x">QuickTime 3.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: QuickTime 3.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The release of QuickTime 3.0 for Mac OS on March 30, 1998 introduced the now-standard revenue model of releasing the software for free, but with additional features of the Apple-provided MoviePlayer application that end-users could only unlock by buying a QuickTime Pro <a href="/wiki/License" title="License">license</a> code. Since the "Pro" features were the same as the existing features in QuickTime 2.5, any previous user of QuickTime could continue to use an older version of the central MoviePlayer application for the remaining lifespan of Mac OS to 2002; indeed, since these additional features were limited to MoviePlayer, any other QuickTime-compatible application remained unaffected.</p>
<p>QuickTime 3.0 added support for graphics importer components that could read images from <a href="/wiki/GIF" title="GIF">GIF</a>, JPEG, <a href="/wiki/TIFF" title="TIFF">TIFF</a> and other file formats, and video output components which served primarily to export movie data via FireWire. Apple also licensed several third-party technologies for inclusion in QuickTime 3.0, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sorenson_Video" title="Sorenson Video">Sorenson Video</a> codec for advanced video compression, the <a href="/wiki/QDesign" title="QDesign">QDesign</a> Music codec for substantial audio compression, and the complete Roland Sound Canvas instrument set and GS Format extensions for improved playback of MIDI music files. It also added video <i>effects</i> which programmers could apply in real-time to video tracks. Some of these effects would even respond to mouse clicks by the user, as part of the new movie <a href="/wiki/Interactivity" title="Interactivity">interaction</a> support (known as <b>wired movies</b>).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_interactive">QuickTime interactive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: QuickTime interactive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the development cycle for QuickTime 3.0, part of the engineering team was working on a more advanced version of QuickTime to be known as <b>QuickTime interactive</b> or QTi. Although similar in concept to the wired movies feature released as part of QuickTime 3.0, QuickTime interactive was much more ambitious. It allowed any QuickTime movie to be a fully interactive and programmable container for media. A special track type was added that contained an interpreter for a custom programming language based on 68000 <a href="/wiki/Assembly_language" title="Assembly language">assembly language</a>. This supported a comprehensive user interaction model for mouse and keyboard event handling based in part on the AML language from the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Media_Tool" title="Apple Media Tool">Apple Media Tool</a>.</p>
<p>The QuickTime interactive movie was to have been the playback format for the next generation of <a href="/wiki/HyperCard" title="HyperCard">HyperCard</a> authoring tool. Both the QuickTime interactive and the HyperCard 3.0 projects were canceled in order to concentrate engineering resources on streaming support for QuickTime 4.0, and the projects were never released to the public.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_4.x">QuickTime 4.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: QuickTime 4.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Apple released QuickTime 4.0 on June 8, 1999<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-32">[32]</a></sup> for Mac OS 7.5.5 through 8.6 (later <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_9" title="Mac OS 9">Mac OS 9</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Windows_95" title="Windows 95">Windows 95</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_98" title="Windows 98">Windows 98</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT" title="Windows NT">Windows NT</a>. Three minor updates (versions 4.0.1, 4.0.2, and 4.0.3) followed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It introduced features that most users now consider basic:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Graphics exporter components, which could write some of the same formats that the previously introduced importers could read. (GIF support was omitted, possibly because of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LZW#Patent_issues" title="LZW">LZW patent</a>.)</li>
<li>Support for the QDesign Music 2 and MPEG-1 Layer 3 audio (MP3).</li>
<li>QuickTime 4 was the first version to support <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streaming</a>. It was accompanied by the release of the free <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_Streaming_Server" title="QuickTime Streaming Server">QuickTime Streaming Server</a> version 1.0.</li>
<li>QuickTime 4 Player introduced <a href="/wiki/Brushed_metal_(interface)" title="Brushed metal (interface)">brushed metal</a> to the Macintosh user interface.</li>
</ul>
<p>On December 17, 1999, Apple provided QuickTime 4.1, this version's first major update.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-32">[32]</a></sup> Two minor versions (4.1.1 and 4.1.2) followed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The most notable improvements in the 4.1.x family were:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Support for files larger than 2.0 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigabytes" title="Gigabytes">GB</a> in Mac OS 9. (This is a consequence of Mac OS 9 requiring the <a href="/wiki/HFS_Plus" title="HFS Plus">HFS Plus</a> filesystem.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Variable_bit_rate" title="Variable bit rate">Variable bit rate</a> (VBR) support for MPEG-1 Layer 3 (MP3) audio.</li>
<li>Support for <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_Multimedia_Integration_Language" title="Synchronized Multimedia Integration Language">Synchronized Multimedia Integration Language</a> (SMIL).</li>
<li>Introduction of AppleScript support in Mac OS.</li>
<li>The requirement of a PowerPC processor for Mac OS systems. QuickTime 4.1 dropped support for Motorola <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/68k" title="68k">68k</a> Macintosh systems.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_5.x">QuickTime 5.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: QuickTime 5.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>QuickTime 5 was one of the shortest-lived versions of QuickTime, released in April 2001 and superseded by QuickTime 6 a little over a year later. This version was the last to have greater capabilities under Mac OS 9 than under Mac OS X, and the last version of QuickTime to support Mac OS versions 7.5.5 through 8.5.1 on a PowerPC Mac and Windows 95. Version 5.0 was initially only released for Mac OS and Mac OS X on April 14, 2001, and version 5.0.1 followed shortly thereafter on April 23, 2001, supporting the classic Mac OS, Mac OS X, and Windows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Three more updates to QuickTime 5 (versions 5.0.2, 5.0.4, and 5.0.5) were released over its short lifespan.</p>
<p>QuickTime 5 delivered the following enhancements:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>MPEG-1 playback for Windows, and updated MPEG-1 Layer 3 audio support for all systems.</li>
<li>Sorenson Video 3 playback and export<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> (added with the 5.0.2 update).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>Realtime rendering of effects &amp; transitions in DV files, including enhancements to DV rendering, multiprocessor support, and Altivec enhancements for <a href="/wiki/PowerPC_G4" title="PowerPC G4">PowerPC G4</a> systems.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macromedia_Flash" title="Macromedia Flash">Flash</a> 4 playback and export.</li>
<li>A new QuickTime VR engine, adding support for cubic VR panoramas.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_6.x">QuickTime 6.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: QuickTime 6.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On July 15, 2002, Apple released QuickTime 6.0, providing the following features:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/MPEG-4" title="MPEG-4">MPEG-4</a> playback, import, and export, including <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4_Part_2" title="MPEG-4 Part 2">MPEG-4 Part 2</a> video and <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="Advanced Audio Coding">AAC Audio</a>.</li>
<li>Support for Flash 5, <a href="/wiki/JPEG_2000" title="JPEG 2000">JPEG 2000</a>, and improved <a href="/wiki/Exif" title="Exif">Exif</a> handling.</li>
<li>Instant-on streaming playback.</li>
<li>MPEG-2 playback (via the purchase of Apple's MPEG-2 Playback Component).</li>
<li>Scriptable <a href="/wiki/ActiveX" title="ActiveX">ActiveX</a> control.</li>
</ul>
<p>QuickTime 6 was initially available for Mac OS 8.6 – 9.x, Mac OS X (10.1.5 minimum), and Windows 98, Me, 2000, and XP. Development of QuickTime 6 for Mac OS slowed considerably in early 2003, after the release of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_v10.2" title="Mac OS X v10.2">Mac OS X v10.2</a> in August 2002. QuickTime 6 for Mac OS continued on the 6.0.x path, eventually stopping with version 6.0.3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 6.1 &amp; 6.1.1 for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_v10.1" title="Mac OS X v10.1">Mac OS X v10.1</a> and Mac OS X v10.2 (released October 22, 2002)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> and QuickTime 6.1 for Windows (released March 31, 2003)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> offered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISO_standard" title="ISO standard">ISO</a>-Compliant MPEG-4 file creation and fixed the <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060323141000/http://archives.neohapsis.com/archives/vulnwatch/2003-q1/0166.html" rel="nofollow">CAN-2003-0168</a> vulnerability.</p>
<p>Apple released QuickTime 6.2 exclusively for Mac OS X on April 29, 2003 to provide support for iTunes 4, which allowed AAC encoding for songs in the iTunes library.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> (iTunes was not available for Windows until October 2003.)</p>
<p>On June 3, 2003, Apple released QuickTime 6.3, delivering the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Support for <a href="/wiki/3GPP" title="3GPP">3GPP</a>, including <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> Text, video, and audio (AAC and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adaptive_Multi-Rate" title="Adaptive Multi-Rate">AMR</a> codecs).</li>
<li>Support for the .3gp, .amr, and .sdv file formats via separate component.</li>
</ul>
<p>QuickTime 6.4, released on October 16, 2003 for Mac OS X v10.2, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_v10.3" title="Mac OS X v10.3">Mac OS X v10.3</a>, and Windows, added the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Addition of the Apple <a href="/wiki/Pixlet" title="Pixlet">Pixlet</a> codec (only for Mac OS X v10.3 and later).</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ColorSync" title="ColorSync">ColorSync</a> support.</li>
<li>Integrated <a href="/wiki/3GPP" title="3GPP">3GPP</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>On December 18, 2003, Apple released QuickTime 6.5, supporting the same systems as version 6.4. Versions 6.5.1 and 6.5.2 followed on April 28, 2004 and October 27, 2004. These versions would be the last to support Windows 98 and Me. The 6.5 family added the following features:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3GP" title="3GP">3GP</a>P2 and AMC mobile multimedia formats.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/QCELP" title="QCELP">QCELP</a> voice code.</li>
<li>Apple Lossless (in version 6.5.1<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>).</li>
</ul>
<p>QuickTime 6.5.3 was released on October 12, 2005 for Mac OS X v10.2.8 after the release of QuickTime 7.0, fixing a number of security issues.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_7.x">QuickTime 7.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: QuickTime 7.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Initially released on April 29, 2005 in conjunction with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_v10.4" title="Mac OS X v10.4">Mac OS X v10.4</a> (for version 10.3.9 and 10.4.x), QuickTime 7.0 featured the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Improved MPEG-4 compliance.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/H.264/MPEG-4_AVC" title="H.264/MPEG-4 AVC">H.264/MPEG-4 AVC</a> codec (does not support the <a href="/wiki/AVCHD" title="AVCHD">AVCHD</a> H.264 AVC format from Sony HD camcorders).</li>
<li>Support for <i><a href="/wiki/Core_Audio" title="Core Audio">Core Audio</a></i>, a set of <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">Application programming interfaces</a> that supports high resolution sound and replaces <a href="/wiki/Sound_Manager" title="Sound Manager">Sound Manager</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>Support for using <a href="/wiki/Core_Image" title="Core Image">Core Image</a> filters in Mac OS X v10.4 on live video (Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Core_Video" title="Core Video">Core Video</a>).</li>
<li>Support for <a href="/wiki/Quartz_Composer" title="Quartz Composer">Quartz Composer</a> (.qtz) animations.</li>
<li>Support for distinct decode order and display order.</li>
<li><i>QuickTime Kit Framework</i> (<i>QTKit</i>), a <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_(API)" title="Cocoa (API)">Cocoa</a> framework for QuickTime.</li>
</ul>
<p>After a couple of preview Windows releases,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Apple released 7.0.2 as the first stable release on September 7, 2005 for <a href="/wiki/Windows_2000" title="Windows 2000">Windows 2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windows_XP" title="Windows XP">Windows XP</a>. Version 7.0.4, released on January 10, 2006 was the first <a href="/wiki/Universal_binary" title="Universal binary">universal binary</a> version. But it suffered numerous bugs, including a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffer_overrun" title="Buffer overrun">buffer overrun</a>, which is more problematic to most users.</p>
<p>Apple dropped support for Windows 2000 with the release of QuickTime 7.2 on July 11, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The last version available for Windows 2000, 7.1.6, contains numerous security vulnerabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> References to this version have been removed from the QuickTime site, but it can be downloaded from Apple's support section.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Apple has not indicated that they will be providing any further security updates for older versions. QuickTime 7.2 is the first version for Windows Vista.</p>
<p>Apple dropped support for Flash content in QuickTime 7.3, breaking content that relied on Flash for interactivity, or animation tracks. Security concerns seem to be part of the decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Flash flv files can still be played in QuickTime if the free <a href="/wiki/Perian" title="Perian">Perian</a> plugin is added.</p>
<p>In QuickTime 7.3, a <a href="/wiki/Central_processing_unit" title="Central processing unit">processor</a> that supports <a href="/wiki/Streaming_SIMD_Extensions" title="Streaming SIMD Extensions">SSE</a> is required. QuickTime 7.4 does not require SSE. Unlike versions 7.2 and 7.3, QuickTime 7.4 cannot be installed on Windows XP SP1 system (its setup program checks if Service Pack 2 is installed).</p>
<p>QuickTime 7.5 was released on June 10, 2008.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> QuickTime 7.5.5 was released on September 9, 2008,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> which requires Mac OS X v10.4 or higher, dropping 10.3 support. QuickTime 7.6 was released on January 21, 2009.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> QuickTime 7.7 was released on August 23, 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7.6.6 is available for OS X, 10.6.3 Snow Leopard through the current, 10.11 El Capitan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7.7.3_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-7.7.3-59">[59]</a></sup> There is a 7.7 release of QuickTime 7 for OS X, but it is only for Leopard 10.5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7.7.6 is the last release for Windows XP.</p>
<p>QuickTime 7.7.9 is the last Windows release of QuickTime. Apple stopped supporting QuickTime on Windows afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windows_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Windows-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_X_.28QuickTime_Player_v10.x.29">QuickTime X (QuickTime Player v10.x)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: QuickTime X (QuickTime Player v10.x)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>QuickTime X (pronounced <i>QuickTime Ten</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>) was initially demonstrated at <a href="/wiki/Apple_Worldwide_Developers_Conference" title="Apple Worldwide Developers Conference">WWDC</a> on June 8, 2009, and shipped with <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Snow_Leopard" title="Mac OS X Snow Leopard">Mac OS X v10.6</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qtx-released-sr_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-qtx-released-sr-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>It includes visual chapters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> conversion, sharing to YouTube, video editing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> capture of video and audio streams, screen recording,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> GPU acceleration, and live streaming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>But it removed support for various widely used formats; in particular the omission of MIDI caused significant inconvenience and trouble to many musicians and their potential audiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, a screen recorder is featured which records whatever is on the screen. However, to prevent <a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording">bootlegging</a> the user is unable to record any video that is played on the DVD Player or purchased content from iTunes, thus being greyed out.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The reason for the jump in numbering from 7 to 10 (X) was to indicate a similar break with the previous versions of the product that Mac OS X indicated. QuickTime X is fundamentally different from previous versions, in that it is provided as a Cocoa (Objective-C) framework and breaks compatibility with the previous QuickTime 7 C-based APIs that were previously used. QuickTime X was completely rewritten to implement modern audio video codecs in 64-bit. QuickTime X is a combination of two technologies: QuickTime Kit Framework (QTKit) and QuickTime X Player. QTKit is used by QuickTime player to display media. QuickTime X does not implement all of the functionality of the previous QuickTime as well as some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (July 2010)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> of the codecs. When QuickTime X attempts to operate with a 32-bit codec or perform an operation not supported by QuickTime X, it will start a 32-bit helper process to perform the requested operation. The website <i><a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a></i> revealed that QuickTime X uses QuickTime 7.x via QTKit to run older codecs that have not made the transition to 64-bit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7 may still be required to support older formats on Snow Leopard such as QTVR, interactive QuickTime movies, and MIDI files. In such cases, a compatible version of QuickTime 7 is included on Snow Leopard installation disc and may be installed side-by-side with QuickTime X. Users who have a Pro license for QuickTime 7 can then activate their license.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>A Snow Leopard compatible version of QuickTime 7 may also be downloaded from Apple Support website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The software got an increment with the release of Mavericks, and as of June 2015, the current version is v10.4. It contains more sharing options (email, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flickr" title="Flickr">Flickr</a> etc.), more export options (including web export in multiple sizes, and export for iPhone 4/iPad/Apple TV (but not Apple TV 2) <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>). It also includes a new way of fast forwarding through a video, magic mouse support for scrolling.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Creating_software_that_uses_QuickTime">Creating software that uses QuickTime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Creating software that uses QuickTime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QuickTime_X">QuickTime X</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: QuickTime X">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(March 2013)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>QuickTime X provides the QTKit Framework on Mac OS 10.6 and greater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Previous_versions">Previous versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Previous versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>QuickTime consists of two major subsystems: the <b>Movie Toolbox</b> and the <b>Image Compression Manager</b>. The Movie Toolbox consists of a general API for handling time-based data, while the Image Compression Manager provides services for dealing with compressed <a href="/wiki/Raster_graphics" title="Raster graphics">raster</a> data as produced by video and photo codecs.</p>
<p>Developers can use the QuickTime software development kit (<a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">SDK</a>) to develop multimedia applications for Mac or Windows with the <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C programming language</a> or with the Java programming language (see <a href="/wiki/QuickTime_for_Java" title="QuickTime for Java">QuickTime for Java</a>), or, under Windows, using <a href="/wiki/Component_Object_Model" title="Component Object Model">COM</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Activex" title="Activex">ActiveX</a> from a language supporting this.</p>
<p>The COM/ActiveX option was introduced as part of QuickTime 7 for Windows and is intended for programmers who want to build standalone Windows applications using high-level QuickTime movie playback and control with some import, export, and editing capabilities. This is considerably easier than mastering the original QuickTime C API.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7 for Mac introduced the QuickTime Kit (aka QTKit), a developer framework that is intended to replace previous APIs for Cocoa developers. This framework is for Mac only, and exists as <a href="/wiki/Objective-C" title="Objective-C">Objective-C</a> abstractions around a subset of the C interface. Mac OS X v10.5 extends QTKit to full 64-bit support. The QTKit allows multiplexing between QuickTime X and QuickTime 7 behind the scenes so that the user need not worry about which version of QuickTime they need to use.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bugs_and_vulnerabilities">Bugs and vulnerabilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=QuickTime&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Bugs and vulnerabilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>QuickTime 7.4 was found to disable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adobe_Software" title="Adobe Software">Adobe</a>'s video compositing program, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_After_Effects" title="Adobe After Effects">After Effects</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> This was due to the <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">DRM</a> built into version 7.4 since it allowed movie rentals from iTunes. QuickTime 7.4.1 resolved this issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Versions 4.0 through 7.3 contained a buffer overflow bug which could compromise the security of a PC using either the QuickTime Streaming Media client, or the QuickTime player itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The bug was fixed in version 7.3.1.</p>
<p>QuickTime 7.5.5 and earlier are known to have a list of significant vulnerabilities that allow a remote attacker to execute arbitrary code or cause a denial of service (out-of-bounds memory access and application crash) on a targeted system. The list includes six types of buffer overflow,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> data conversion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> signed vs unsigned integer mismatch,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and uninitialized memory pointer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7.6 has been found to disable Macintosh users' ability to play certain games, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Civilization_IV" title="Civilization IV">Civilization IV</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sims_2" title="The Sims 2">The Sims 2</a></i>. There are fixes available from the publisher, <a href="/wiki/Aspyr" title="Aspyr">Aspyr</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7 lacks support for H.264 Sample Aspect Ratio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> QuickTime X does not have this limitation,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> but many Apple products (such as <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a>) still use the older QuickTime 7 engine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>QuickTime 7.7.x on Windows fails to encode H.264 on Dual CPU systems with more than approximately 20 threads, e.g. HP Z820 with 2x 8-core CPUs. A suggested solution<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (April 2016)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> is to disable hyper-threading/limit CPU cores. Encoding speed and stability depends on the scaling of the player window.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On April 14, 2016, Christopher Budd of <a href="/wiki/Trend_Micro" title="Trend Micro">Trend Micro</a> announced that Apple has ceased all security patching of QuickTime for Windows, and called attention to two Zero Day Initiative advisories, ZDI-16-241 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and ZDI-16-242, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> issued by Trend Micro's subsidiary <a href="/wiki/TippingPoint" title="TippingPoint">TippingPoint</a> on that same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Also on that same day, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Computer_Emergency_Readiness_Team" title="United States Computer Emergency Readiness Team">United States Computer Emergency Readiness Team</a> issued alert TA16-105A, encapsulating Budd's announcement and the Zero Day Initiative advisories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Apple responded with a statement that QuickTime 7 for Windows is no longer supported by Apple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windows_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Windows-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
